# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy Listener Manager Lifecycle Architecture

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the listener manager: the listener addition/removal API, the listener drain mechanism, the connection handler assignment to worker threads, and the listener socket sharing between workers.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented all the C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the listener manager. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've created a comprehensive JSON file at `/workspace/answer.json` containing **45 C++ source files** that implement the Envoy listener manager architecture:

### Key Components Found:

**1. Core Listener Management (listener_manager_impl, listener_impl)**
- Handles listener addition/removal API
- Manages listener state transitions (ACTIVE → WARMING → DRAINING)
- Implements dynamic listener updates via `addOrUpdateListener()`, `removeListener()`

**2. Listener Drain Mechanism**
- `DrainingListener` and `DrainingFilterChainsManager` classes track listeners being drained
- `DrainManagerImpl` coordinates graceful drain sequences
- Tracks `workers_pending_removal_` count for coordinated shutdown

**3. Connection Handler & Worker Assignment**
- `ConnectionHandlerImpl` routes incoming connections to worker threads
- `WorkerImpl` represents worker threads with their own `Event::Dispatcher`
- `ActiveStreamListenerBase` and derived classes accept connections per worker

**4. Socket Sharing Between Workers**
- SO_REUSEPORT socket option for per-worker sockets
- `listen_socket_impl`, `tcp_listener_impl`, `udp_listener_impl` handle socket creation
- `BindType::ReusePort` and `BindType::NoReusePort` control socket sharing strategy

**5. Supporting Components**
- LDS API for dynamic listener discovery
- Filter chain manager for in-place updates
- Active listener implementations for TCP, UDP, QUIC protocols
- Server integration and API listener support

The detailed `text` field in the JSON provides a comprehensive narrative explaining how these components work together to implement the listener manager li

Manages drain timeouts and sequences\\n   - Implements Network::DrainDecision for flow control during drain\\n\\n3. **Listener draining flow**:\\n   - When a listener is removed or updated, it transitions to DRAINING state\\n   - Draining listeners continue to accept existing connections but stop accepting new ones\\n   - Workers notify the listener manager when they complete draining via callbacks\\n   - Once all workers have drained, the listener is destroyed\\n\\n## Connection Handler Assignment to Worker Threads\\n\\nThe connection handler and worker assignment is implemented through:\\n\\n1. **ConnectionHandler** (`source/common/listener_manager/connection_handler_impl.h/cc`, `envoy/network/connection_handler.h`):\\n   - Workers register listeners via `addListener()` which posts to the worker's dispatcher\\n   - Connections are assigned to workers deterministically (round-robin or kernel affinity via SO_REUSEPORT)\\n\\n3. **Active listeners** (`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.h/cc`):\\n   - for managing network listeners with the following key components:\\n\\n## Listener Addition/Removal API\\n\\nThe core API is defined in `envoy/server/listener_manager.h` (ListenerManager interface) and implemented in `source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h/cc`. The ListenerManagerImpl class provides:\\n\\n- `addOrUpdateListener()`: Adds or updates a listener configuration, supporting dynamic listener management\\n- `removeListener()`: Removes a listener by name\\n- `beginListenerUpdate()` / `endListenerUpdate()`: Lifecycle methods for updating listener configurations\\n- `listeners()`: Returns listeners in various states (ACTIVE, WARMING, DRAINING)\\n\\nSpecific listener implementations are in `source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.h/cc` (ListenerImpl class).\\n\\n## Listener Drain Mechanism\\n\\nThe drain mechanism is implemented through:\\n\\n1. **ListenerManagerImpl drain management** (`source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h/cc`):\\n   - Maintains `draining_listeners_` list of DrainingListener objects\\n   - Maintains `draining_filter_chains_manager_` list of DrainingFilterChainsManager objects\\n   - Manages the transition of listeners from ACTIVE to DRAINING state\\n   - Tracks `workers_pending_removal_` count for each draining listener\\n\\n2. **DrainManager** (`source/server/drain_manager_impl.h/cc`):\\n   - Implements the Server::DrainManager interface\\n   - Coordinates graceful draining with `startDrainSequence()`\\n   - Manages drain timeouts and sequences\\n   - Implements Network::DrainDecision for flow control during drain\\n\\n3. **Listener draining flow**:\\n   - When a listener is removed or updated, it transitions to DRAINING state\\n   - Draining listeners continue to accept existing connections but stop accepting new ones\\n   - Workers notify the listener manager when they complete draining via callbacks\\n   - Once all workers have drained, the listener is destroyed\\n\\n## Connection Handler Assignment to Worker Threads\\n\\nThe connection handler and worker assignment is implemented through:\\n\\n1. **ConnectionHandler** (`source/common/listener_manager/connection_handler_impl.h/cc`, `envoy/network/connection_handler.h`):\\n   - ConnectionHandlerImpl receives incoming connections from the kernel\\n   - Routes connections to appropriate worker threads based on configuration\\n   - Implements Network::ConnectionHandler interface\\n   - Manages per-worker connection dispatchers\\n\\n2. **Worker threads** (`source/server/worker_impl.h/cc`):\\n   - WorkerImpl represents a single worker thread\\n   - Each worker has its own Event::Dispatcher for asynchronous I/O\\n   - Workers register listeners via `addListener()` which posts to the worker's dispatcher\\n   - Connections are assigned to workers deterministically (round-robin or kernel affinity via SO_REUSEPORT)\\n\\n3. **Active listeners** (`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.h/cc`):\\n   - ActiveStreamListenerBase handles accepting connections on a listener socket\\n   - Manages active connections and filter chains\\n   - Derived classes: ActiveTcpListener, ActiveQuicListener, etc.\\n   - Runs on worker thread dispatcher, posting work via `dispatcher.post()`\\n\\n## Listener Socket Sharing Between Workers\\n\\nSocket sharing is controlled through the SO_REUSEPORT mechanism:\\n\\n1. **Socket creation** (`source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.h/cc`):\\n   - Creates one socket per worker when `use_original_dst` or `per_connection_buffer_limit_bytes` requires it\\n   - Checks for SO_REUSEPORT support in `listener_impl.cc`\\n   - Creates sockets via ListenerComponentFactory::createListenSocket()\\n\\n2. **Socket binding types** (`envoy/server/listener_manager.h`):\\n   - ListenerComponentFactory::BindType::NoReusePort: Single shared socket\\n   - ListenerComponentFactory::BindType::ReusePort: Each worker gets its own socket with SO_REUSEPORT\\n   - Controlled by listener configuration and concurrency settings\\n\\n3. **Listen socket implementations** (`source/common/network/listen_socket_impl.h/cc`):\\n   - TcpListenSocket: TCP listener socket with port binding\\n   - UdpListenSocket: UDP listener socket\\n   - BaseListenerImpl: Base class for TCP/UDP sockets\\n   - TcpListenerImpl / UdpListenerImpl: Concrete socket implementations\\n\\n4. **SO_REUSEPORT handling** (`source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.cc`):\\n   - Sets SO_REUSEPORT socket option when configured\\n   - Required for UDP listeners with concurrency > 1 (kernel hash to consistent worker)\\n   - Allows kernel to distribute incoming packets to multiple worker sockets\\n   - Handles socket option creation in `source/common/network/socket_option_factory.cc`\\n\\n## Integration Points\\n\\n1. **Server integration** (`source/server/server.h/cc`):\\n   - Server instance creates and owns ListenerManager\\n   - Manages listener manager lifecycle\\n   - Coordinates with other subsystems (cluster manager, dispatcher, etc.)\\n\\n2. **LDS API** (`source/common/listener_manager/lds_api.h/cc`):\\n   - Discovers listener configurations from control plane\\n   - Calls `addOrUpdateListener()` and `removeListener()` on ListenerManager\\n   - Handles version tracking and xDS subscription\\n\\n3. **Filter chains** (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h/cc`):\\n   - Manages filter chains within a listener\\n   - Supports in-place filter chain updates\\n   - Drains filter chains when listeners are updated\\n\\n4. **API listeners** (`source/server/api_listener_impl.h/cc`):\\n   - Separate listener type for xDS/gRPC APIs\\n   - Managed independently from network listeners\\n\\n5. **Validation listener manager** (`source/extensions/listener_managers/validation_listener_manager/`):\\n   - Lightweight listener manager for config validation\\n   - Used during configuration loading without starting actual listeners\"\n}\n",

TcpListenSocket: TCP listener socket with port binding\\n   - UdpListenSocket: UDP listener socket\\n   - BaseListenerImpl: Base class for TCP/UDP sockets\\n   - TcpListenerImpl / UdpListenerImpl: Concrete socket implementations\\n\\n4. **SO_REUSEPORT handling** (`source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.cc`):\\n   - Sets SO_REUSEPORT socket option when configured\\n   - Required for UDP listeners with concurrency > 1 (kernel hash to consistent worker)\\n   - Allows kernel to distribute incoming packets to multiple worker sockets\\n   - Handles socket option creation in `source/common/network/socket_option_factory.cc`\\n\\n## Integration Points\\n\\n1. **Server integration** (`source/server/server.h/cc`):\\n   - Server instance creates and owns ListenerManager\\n   - Manages listener manager lifecycle\\n   - Coordinates with other subsystems (cluster manager, dispatcher, etc.)\\n\\n2. **LDS API** (`source/common/listener_manager/lds_api.h/cc`):\\n   - Discovers listener configurations from control plane\\n   - Calls `addOrUpdateListener()` and `removeListener()` on ListenerManager\\n   - Handles version tracking and xDS subscription\\n\\n3. **Filter chains** (`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h/cc`):\\n   - Manages filter chains within a listener\\n   - Supports in-place filter chain updates\\n   - Drains filter chains when listeners are updated\\n\\n4. **API listeners** (`source/server/api_listener_impl.h/cc`):\\n   - Separate listener type for xDS/gRPC APIs\\n   - Managed independently from network listeners\\n\\n5. **Validation listener manager** (`source/extensions/listener_managers/validation_listener_manager/`):\\n   - Lightweight listener manager for config validation\\n   - Used during configuration loading without starting actual listeners\"\n}\n",
